\DoxyCodeLine{00058\ \textcolor{comment}{/*\ This\ file\ is\ for\ inclusion\ into\ client\ (your!)\ code.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00059\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00060\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ You\ can\ use\ these\ macros\ to\ manipulate\ and\ query\ Valgrind's\ }}
\DoxyCodeLine{00061\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ execution\ inside\ your\ own\ programs.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00062\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00063\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ The\ resulting\ executables\ will\ still\ run\ without\ Valgrind,\ just\ a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00064\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ little\ bit\ more\ slowly\ than\ they\ otherwise\ would,\ but\ otherwise}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00065\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ unchanged.\ \ When\ not\ running\ on\ valgrind,\ each\ client\ request}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00066\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ consumes\ very\ few\ (eg.\ 7)\ instructions,\ so\ the\ resulting\ performance}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00067\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ loss\ is\ negligible\ unless\ you\ plan\ to\ execute\ client\ requests}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00068\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ millions\ of\ times\ per\ second.\ \ Nevertheless,\ if\ that\ is\ still\ a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00069\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ problem,\ you\ can\ compile\ with\ the\ NVALGRIND\ symbol\ defined\ (gcc}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00070\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ -\/DNVALGRIND)\ so\ that\ client\ requests\ are\ not\ even\ compiled\ in.\ \ */}}

\DoxyCodeLine{00083\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ identifying\ architectures,\ which\ are\ different\ to\ the\ ones\ we\ use}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00084\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ within\ the\ rest\ of\ Valgrind.\ \ Note,\ \_\_powerpc\_\_\ is\ active\ for\ both}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00085\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ 32\ and\ 64-\/bit\ PPC,\ whereas\ \_\_powerpc64\_\_\ is\ only\ active\ for\ the}}

\DoxyCodeLine{00122\ \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#if\ defined(NVALGRIND)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00123\ }
\DoxyCodeLine{00124\ \textcolor{comment}{/*\ Define\ NVALGRIND\ to\ completely\ remove\ the\ Valgrind\ magic\ sequence}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00125\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ from\ the\ compiled\ code\ (analogous\ to\ NDEBUG's\ effects\ on}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00126\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ assert())\ */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00127\ \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#define\ VALGRIND\_DO\_CLIENT\_REQUEST(\_zzq\_rlval,\ \_zzq\_default,\ \_zzq\_request,\ \_zzq\_arg1,\ \_zzq\_arg2,\ \(\backslash\)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00128\ \textcolor{preprocessor}{\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \_zzq\_arg3,\ \_zzq\_arg4,\ \_zzq\_arg5)\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \(\backslash\)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00129\ \textcolor{preprocessor}{\ \ \ \ \{\ (\_zzq\_rlval)\ =\ (\_zzq\_default);\ \}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00130\ }
\DoxyCodeLine{00131\ \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#else\ }\textcolor{comment}{/*\ !\ NVALGRIND\ */}\textcolor{preprocessor}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00132\ }
\DoxyCodeLine{00133\ \textcolor{comment}{/*\ The\ following\ defines\ the\ magic\ code\ sequences\ which\ the\ JITter}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00134\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ spots\ and\ handles\ magically.\ \ Don't\ look\ too\ closely\ at\ them\ as}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00135\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ they\ will\ rot\ your\ brain.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00136\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00137\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ The\ assembly\ code\ sequences\ for\ all\ architectures\ is\ in\ this\ one}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00138\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ file.\ \ This\ is\ because\ this\ file\ must\ be\ stand-\/alone,\ and\ we\ don't}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00139\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ want\ to\ have\ multiple\ files.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00140\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00141\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ For\ VALGRIND\_DO\_CLIENT\_REQUEST,\ we\ must\ ensure\ that\ the\ default}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00142\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ value\ gets\ put\ in\ the\ return\ slot,\ so\ that\ everything\ works\ when}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00143\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ this\ is\ executed\ not\ under\ Valgrind.\ \ Args\ are\ passed\ in\ a\ memory}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00144\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ block,\ and\ so\ there's\ no\ intrinsic\ limit\ to\ the\ number\ that\ could}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00145\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ be\ passed,\ but\ it's\ currently\ five.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00146\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ }}
\DoxyCodeLine{00147\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ The\ macro\ args\ are:\ }}
\DoxyCodeLine{00148\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ \ \ \ \_zzq\_rlval\ \ \ \ result\ lvalue}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00149\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ \ \ \ \_zzq\_default\ \ default\ value\ (result\ returned\ when\ running\ on\ real\ CPU)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00150\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ \ \ \ \_zzq\_request\ \ request\ code}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00151\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ \ \ \ \_zzq\_arg1..5\ \ request\ params}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00152\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00153\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ The\ other\ two\ macros\ are\ used\ to\ support\ function\ wrapping,\ and\ are}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00154\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ a\ lot\ simpler.\ \ VALGRIND\_GET\_NR\_CONTEXT\ returns\ the\ value\ of\ the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00155\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ guest's\ NRADDR\ pseudo-\/register\ and\ whatever\ other\ information\ is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00156\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ needed\ to\ safely\ run\ the\ call\ original\ from\ the\ wrapper:\ on}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00157\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ ppc64-\/linux,\ the\ R2\ value\ at\ the\ divert\ point\ is\ also\ needed.\ \ This}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00158\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ information\ is\ abstracted\ into\ a\ user-\/visible\ type,\ OrigFn.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00159\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00160\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ VALGRIND\_CALL\_NOREDIR\_*\ behaves\ the\ same\ as\ the\ following\ on\ the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00161\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ guest,\ but\ guarantees\ that\ the\ branch\ instruction\ will\ not\ be}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00162\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ redirected:\ x86:\ call\ *\%eax,\ amd64:\ call\ *\%rax,\ ppc32/ppc64:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00163\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ branch-\/and-\/link-\/to-\/r11.\ \ VALGRIND\_CALL\_NOREDIR\ is\ just\ text,\ not\ a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00164\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ complete\ inline\ asm,\ since\ it\ needs\ to\ be\ combined\ with\ more\ magic}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00165\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ inline\ asm\ stuff\ to\ be\ useful.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00166\ \textcolor{comment}{*/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00167\ }
\DoxyCodeLine{00168\ \textcolor{comment}{/*\ -\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/\ x86-\/linux\ -\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/-\/\ */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00169\ }

\DoxyCodeLine{00524\ \textcolor{comment}{/*\ This\ section\ defines\ magic\ (a.k.a\ appalling-\/hack)\ macros\ for\ doing}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00525\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ guaranteed-\/no-\/redirection\ macros,\ so\ as\ to\ get\ from\ function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00526\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ wrappers\ to\ the\ functions\ they\ are\ wrapping.\ \ The\ whole\ point\ is\ to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00527\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ construct\ standard\ call\ sequences,\ but\ to\ do\ the\ call\ itself\ with\ a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00528\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ special\ no-\/redirect\ call\ pseudo-\/instruction\ that\ the\ JIT}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00529\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ understands\ and\ handles\ specially.\ \ This\ section\ is\ long\ and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00530\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ repetitious,\ and\ I\ can't\ see\ a\ way\ to\ make\ it\ shorter.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00531\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00532\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ The\ naming\ scheme\ is\ as\ follows:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00533\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00534\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ \ \ \ CALL\_FN\_\{W,v\}\_\{v,W,WW,WWW,WWWW,5W,6W,7W,etc\}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00535\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00536\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ 'W'\ stands\ for\ "{}word"{}\ and\ 'v'\ for\ "{}void"{}.\ \ Hence\ there\ are}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00537\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ different\ macros\ for\ calling\ arity\ 0,\ 1,\ 2,\ 3,\ 4,\ etc,\ functions,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00538\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ and\ for\ each,\ the\ possibility\ of\ returning\ a\ word-\/typed\ result,\ or}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00539\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ no\ result.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00540\ \textcolor{comment}{*/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00541\ }

\DoxyCodeLine{00959\ \textcolor{comment}{/*\ NB\ 9\ Sept\ 07.\ \ There\ is\ a\ nasty\ kludge\ here\ in\ all\ these\ CALL\_FN\_}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00960\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ macros.\ \ In\ order\ not\ to\ trash\ the\ stack\ redzone,\ we\ need\ to\ drop}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00961\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ \%rsp\ by\ 128\ before\ the\ hidden\ call,\ and\ restore\ afterwards.\ \ The}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00962\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ nastyness\ is\ that\ it\ is\ only\ by\ luck\ that\ the\ stack\ still\ appears}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00963\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ to\ be\ unwindable\ during\ the\ hidden\ call\ -\/\ since\ then\ the\ behaviour}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00964\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ of\ any\ routine\ using\ this\ macro\ does\ not\ match\ what\ the\ CFI\ data}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00965\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ says.\ \ Sigh.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00966\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00967\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ Why\ is\ this\ important?\ \ Imagine\ that\ a\ wrapper\ has\ a\ stack}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00968\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ allocated\ local,\ and\ passes\ to\ the\ hidden\ call,\ a\ pointer\ to\ it.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00969\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ Because\ gcc\ does\ not\ know\ about\ the\ hidden\ call,\ it\ may\ allocate}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00970\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ that\ local\ in\ the\ redzone.\ \ Unfortunately\ the\ hidden\ call\ may\ then}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00971\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ trash\ it\ before\ it\ comes\ to\ use\ it.\ \ So\ we\ must\ step\ clear\ of\ the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00972\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ redzone,\ for\ the\ duration\ of\ the\ hidden\ call,\ to\ make\ it\ safe.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00973\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{00974\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ Probably\ the\ same\ problem\ afflicts\ the\ other\ redzone-\/style\ ABIs\ too}}

\DoxyCodeLine{03518\ \textcolor{comment}{/*\ These\ requests\ allow\ control\ to\ move\ from\ the\ simulated\ CPU\ to\ the}}

\DoxyCodeLine{03520\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ }}

\DoxyCodeLine{03536\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ any\ global\ variables,\ and\ does\ not\ refer\ to\ any\ libc\ or\ other\ functions}}

\DoxyCodeLine{03538\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ likely\ to\ have\ a\ bad\ outcome,\ for\ tricky\ reasons\ which\ we've\ grappled}}

\DoxyCodeLine{03584\ \textcolor{comment}{/*\ Mark\ a\ block\ of\ memory\ as\ having\ been\ allocated\ by\ a\ malloc()-\/like}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03585\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ function.\ \ `addr'\ is\ the\ start\ of\ the\ usable\ block\ (ie.\ after\ any}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03586\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ redzone)\ `rzB'\ is\ redzone\ size\ if\ the\ allocator\ can\ apply\ redzones;}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03587\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ use\ '0'\ if\ not.\ \ Adding\ redzones\ makes\ it\ more\ likely\ Valgrind\ will\ spot}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03588\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ block\ overruns.\ \ `is\_zeroed'\ indicates\ if\ the\ memory\ is\ zeroed,\ as\ it\ is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03589\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ for\ calloc().\ \ Put\ it\ immediately\ after\ the\ point\ where\ a\ block\ is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03590\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ allocated.\ }}
\DoxyCodeLine{03591\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ }}
\DoxyCodeLine{03592\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ If\ you're\ using\ Memcheck:\ If\ you're\ allocating\ memory\ via\ superblocks,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03593\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ and\ then\ handing\ out\ small\ chunks\ of\ each\ superblock,\ if\ you\ don't\ have}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03594\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ redzones\ on\ your\ small\ blocks,\ it's\ worth\ marking\ the\ superblock\ with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03595\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ VALGRIND\_MAKE\_MEM\_NOACCESS\ when\ it's\ created,\ so\ that\ block\ overruns\ are}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03596\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ detected.\ \ But\ if\ you\ can\ put\ redzones\ on,\ it's\ probably\ better\ to\ not\ do}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03597\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ this,\ so\ that\ messages\ for\ small\ overruns\ are\ described\ in\ terms\ of\ the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03598\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ small\ block\ rather\ than\ the\ superblock\ (but\ if\ you\ have\ a\ big\ overrun}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03599\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ that\ skips\ over\ a\ redzone,\ you\ could\ miss\ an\ error\ this\ way).\ \ See}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03600\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ memcheck/tests/custom\_alloc.c\ for\ an\ example.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03601\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03602\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ WARNING:\ if\ your\ allocator\ uses\ malloc()\ or\ 'new'\ to\ allocate}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03603\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ superblocks,\ rather\ than\ mmap()\ or\ brk(),\ this\ will\ not\ work\ properly\ -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03604\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ you'll\ likely\ get\ assertion\ failures\ during\ leak\ detection.\ \ This\ is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03605\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ because\ Valgrind\ doesn't\ like\ seeing\ overlapping\ heap\ blocks.\ \ Sorry.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03606\ \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{03607\ \textcolor{comment}{\ \ \ Nb:\ block\ must\ be\ freed\ via\ a\ free()-\/like\ function\ specified}}
